CITY OF SAN MATEO
City Council Regular Meeting
August 19, 2024
7:00 PM
City Hall Council Chamber
Entrance is on O’Farrell Street
COUNCIL MEMBERS
Lisa Diaz Nash, Mayor
Rob Newsom Jr., Deputy Mayor
Rich Hedges
Amourence Lee
Adam Loraine
 
AMENDED AGENDA
THIS MEETING CAN BE ATTENDED IN PERSON OR REMOTE BY JOINING ZOOM – SEE CODES BELOW.
PUBLIC COMMENTS WILL BE ACCEPTED BOTH IN PERSON AND REMOTELY.
SEE END OF AGENDA FOR OPTIONS AND INSTRUCTIONS ON HOW TO PARTICIPATE IN THE MEETING. 
To join via Zoom – click here: August 19, 2024
To join via telephone:  (408) 638-0968      
Webinar ID: 854 2538 3708      Passcode: 626417
The City Council meeting will conclude by 11:00 p.m. unless otherwise extended by council vote. 
Any unheard items will automatically move forward to the next regular meeting. 
Item #28 was added to the amended agenda on Friday, August 16, 2024
CALL TO ORDER
Pledge of Allegiance
Roll Call
AB 2449 Requests and Considerations for Meeting Participation by Teleconference due to Just Cause or Emergency
Circumstances
CEREMONIAL
1.
San Mateo American Little League 12U - Recognition
2.
Peninsula Clean Energy Update - Presentation
CONSENT CALENDAR
All matters listed under the Consent Calendar are considered by the Council to be routine and will be enacted by one motion without
discussion. If discussion is desired, that item may be removed and considered separately.
 
3.
State Route 82/State Route 92 Interchange Landscaping Improvements Project – Agreement
Approve an agreement with Marina Landscape, Inc. for the State Route 82/State Route 92 Interchange
Landscaping Improvements Project in the amount of $1,650,150; establish a contingency reserve in the amount
of $250,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form
presented and issue change orders as allowed by the contract documents and within the contingency amount.
CEQA: The landscaping scope of work received environmental clearance when the project level initial study and
negative declaration for the 82/92 Interchange Project was approved in May 2014. Environmental clearance for
the Landscaping Project has been re-validated by Caltrans on September 2, 2021.
4.
Central Recreation Center Roof Improvements – Agreement
1 of 407

--- page 2 ---
Adopt a Resolution approving an alternative purchasing procedure to award an agreement with McGinnis Chen
Associates, Inc. for design professional services in an amount not to exceed $93,025; establish a contingency
reserve of $10,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form
presented and issue amendments within the contingency amount.
CEQA: This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or
former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
5.
1001 Haddon Drive Ponding Repair – Agreement
Approve an agreement with W.R. Forde Associates, Inc. for 1001 Haddon Drive Ponding Repair Project in the
amount of $163,415.00; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $24,500; and authorize the Public
Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders as allowed
by the contract documents and within the amount of the contingency amount.
CEQA: This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or
former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
6.
731 and 771 Crystal Springs Road Access Easements – Acceptance
Adopt Resolutions to accept two Grants of Easement on 731 Crystal Springs Road and 771 Crystal Springs Road;
and authorize the City Manager to execute the Grants of Easement in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: This Project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or
former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
7.
Parks and Recreation Department Field Mowers - Purchase Contract
Adopt a Resolution to approve an alternative purchasing procedure and approve a purchase contract with Turf
Star, Inc. for the purchase of one (1) Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) Toro Z Master Revolution in a total
amount not to exceed $182,782.62; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $30,000.00; and authorize
the Public Works Director to execute the purchase contract in substantially the form presented and issue change
orders within the contingency amount.
CEQA: This purchase is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that there is no
possibility that the purchase of field mowers may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines
Section 15061(b)(3).)
8.
Staff Augmentation Services – Agreement
Approve a professional consultant services agreement to SNG & Associates, Inc. in an amount not to exceed
$200,000; establish a contingency reserve of $20,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the
agreement in substantially the form presented and issue any future amendments within the contingency amount.
CEQA: This Council action is not a project subject to CEQA review under the “common sense” exemption, because
it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that the award of a staff augmentation agreement to
assist the City in managing capital improvement projects may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA
Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
2 of 407

--- page 3 ---
9.
Afterschool Enrichment Services for School Year 2024-2025 – Agreement
Approve an agreement with San Mateo Union High School District for afterschool enrichment services for
Empowerment Through Action (ETA) Program in an amount not to exceed $31,000 starting on August 20, 2024
through May 29, 2025 and authorize Parks and Recreation Director to execute the agreement in substantially the
form presented.
CEQA: This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity
that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)
(5).)
10.
Police Department Roof Improvements – Construction Contract
Adopt a Resolution approving an alternative purchasing procedure to award a construction contract to Angeles
Contractor, Inc. in the amount of $1,607,434.64 for the Police Department Roof Improvements project; establish
a contingency reserve in the amount of $160,000.00; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the
contract in substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
CEQA: This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or
former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
11.
League of California Cities Annual Conference – Voting Delegate Designation
Designate Deputy Mayor Rob Newsom Jr as the City's Voting Delegate and Council Member Rich Hedges as the
alternate for the 2024 League of California Cities Annual Conference.
CEQA: This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that
will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
12.
Community Development Permit Tracking Software – Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 2 to the Agreement with Tyler Technologies, Inc. to convert the existing on-premises
EnerGov Permitting and Licensing software to a cloud-based service hosted by Tyler Technologies; increase the
annual service maintenance/support fee from $90,759 to $194,381; and authorize the Community Development
Director to execute the Amendment in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: This Amendment is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that there is no
possibility that transitioning EnerGov Permitting and Licensing software to cloud-based services will have a
significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
13.
Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade and Expansion Project Easement – Amendment
Adopt a Resolution to approve an amendment to the Easement Deed and Agreement between the City of San
Mateo and All American Self Storage, L.P. modifying the Public Utility Easement for the Wastewater Treatment
Plant site; and authorize the Mayor to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in accordance with the
California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). The PEIR was certified by City Council on June
6, 2016. In accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for
implementation of the Clean Water Program. The City prepared an Addendum to the Final PEIR that were
approved on July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the
project evaluated in the PEIR and Addenda.
3 of 407

--- page 4 ---
14.
Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade and Expansion Project Owner-Controlled Insurance Program – Policy
Extension
Approve an extension to the City’s Owner-Controlled Insurance Program policy with Old Republic General
Insurance Corporation to extend coverage for construction of the Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade and
Expansion Project in an amount not to exceed $1,069,153, for a revised total not to exceed cost of $10,569,153;
approve a contingency reserve in the amount of $350,000 for potential additional extensions; and authorize the
City Manager to approve the policy extension in substantially the form presented and additional policy
extensions within the contingency amount.
CEQA: For the WWTP Project, the City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in
accordance with the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). The PEIR was certified
by City Council on June 6, 2016. In accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental
compliance document for implementation of the Clean Water Program. The City prepared an Addendum to the
Final PEIR that were approved on July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2).
15.
Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade Engineering Services During Construction – Amendment & Contingency
Increase
Approve Amendment No. 11 to the agreement with HDR Engineering, Inc. for additional engineering services
during construction for the Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade and Expansion Project in the amount of
$1,607,808 for a new total agreement amount of $18,095,235; increase the contingency reserve by $320,000 for
a new total contingency amount of $3,664,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the
amendment and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
CEQA: The City prepared a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) in accordance with the
California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). The PEIR was certified by City Council on June
6, 2016. In accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for
implementation of the Clean Water Program. The City prepared an Addendum to the Final PEIR that were
approved on July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2). This work is within the scope of the
project evaluated in the PEIR and Addenda.
16.
High Voltage Streetlight Conversion (Phase 5) Project – Agreement
Approve an agreement with Columbia Electric, Inc. for construction of the High Voltage Streetlight Conversion
(Phase 5) Project in the amount of $2,050,325; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $315,000; and
authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue
change orders as allowed by the contract documents and within contingency amount.
CEQA: This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or
former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
17.
Police Department Radio Replacement – Agreement
Adopt a Resolution to use an alternative purchasing procedure in accordance with Municipal Code Section
3.60.070(h)(3) to approve an agreement with Metro Mobile Communications for the purchase of replacement
handheld and mobile radios for the San Mateo Police Department in the amount of $721,055.83; authorize the
Chief of Police to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented; and authorize the Chief of Police to
issue change orders of up to $50,000 cumulatively and the City Manager to issue change orders in excess of
$50,000 but not to exceed $100,000 cumulatively.
4 of 407

--- page 5 ---
CEQA: This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a
physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
18.
Marina Library Structural Improvements Project – Amendment and Contingency Increase
Approve Amendment No. 4 with Siegel & Strain Architects for design professional services for the Marina Library
Structural Improvements project in an amount not to exceed $506,694 for a new agreement amount of
$903,551; increase the contingency reserve in the amount of $54,000 for a total contingency of $90,000; and
authorize the Public Works Director to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented and any
future amendments within the contingency amount.
CEQA: This Approval of Amendment No. 4 is not a project subject to CEQA, because the work associated with the
Marina Library Structural Improvements Project is categorically exempt as an “existing facility,” in that it consists
of the operation, repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or
private structures, facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no
expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
19.
Tuolumne County Resource Conservation District – Agreement
Approve an agreement for a term from September 2, 2024, to June 30, 2025, with the Tuolumne County
Resource Conservation District for compost procurement services in the amount of $3,600 and authorize the City
Manager to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: An agreement with the Tuolumne County Resource Conservation District to assist the City in procuring
compost to meet the City’s annual compost procurement target is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be
seen with certainty that approval of this agreement will not cause a direct physical change, or a reasonably
foreseeable indirect change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
20.
Police Department Motorcycle Replacement - Contract
Adopt a Resolution to approve an alternative purchasing procedure and approve a purchase contract with
National Auto Fleet Group, a Division of Chevrolet of Watsonville, for the purchase of four (4) new BMW RT 1250
police specification motorcycles in the total amount not to exceed $165,582.83; establish a contingency reserve
in the amount of $20,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to issue change orders and execute the
purchase contract in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: This purchase contract is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that there is
no possibility that the purchase of four replacement police motorcycles may have a significant effect on the
environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
21.
City Wide In-Person Safety Training – Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 2 to the professional consultant services agreement with Du-All Safety, LLC, for in-
person safety training of City employees; increase the agreement by $240,000, for a new not-to-exceed total
amount of $360,000; approve a contingency reserve increase of $40,000, for a new contingency total of $52,000;
extend the term of the agreement through August 31, 2026; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute
the amendment in substantially the form presented and execute amendments within the contingency amount,
including no-cost time extensions.
CEQA: This Council action is exempt from CEQA, in that it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility
that safety training for City employees may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines
Section 15061(b)(3).)
5 of 407

--- page 6 ---
22.
Clean Water Program – Program Management Contingency
Approve an increase to the contingency reserve associated with Amendment No. 9 to the agreement with CH2M
Hill Engineers, Inc., for program management services for the Clean Water Program, in the amount of $250,000,
for a revised contingency reserve of $1,697,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute amendments
within the contingency amount.
CEQA: Council approval of a contingency increase associated with Amendment No. 9 to the Agreement between
the City and CH2M is exempt from CEQA review because the potential use of contingency to increase continued
program management can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that the management services may
have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines section 15061(b)(3).) In addition, the City prepared
a Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) for the Clean Water Program in accordance with
the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) (SCH No. 2015032006). Council on June 6, 2016, certified the
PEIR. In accordance with CEQA, the Final PEIR serves as the primary environmental compliance document for the
implementation of the Clean Water Program. The City prepared Addenda to the Final PEIR that was approved on
July 16, 2018 (Addendum 1) and April 15, 2019 (Addendum 2)
23.
Library Materials Acquisition – Amendment
Approve an amendment to the agreement with Baker & Taylor for a 3-year extension to be the primary vendor to
provide library materials including books, audiobooks, DVDs, CDs and customized collection development
services in the amount not to exceed $500,000 annually for fiscal years 2024-25, 2025-26, and 2026-27 and
authorize the City Manager to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity which does not
involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the
environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
24.
Worker Resource Center at 171 North Amphlett Boulevard – Lease Amendment
Adopt a Resolution to appropriate $5,000 from the General Fund to the Worker Resource Center Fund to cover
the additional cost of leasing the property at 171 North Amphlett Boulevard; approve Amendment No. 1 to the
lease agreement for the property at 171 North Amphlett Boulevard for a period of one year at the rate of
$5,627.54 per month for use as the Worker Resource Center; and authorize the City Manager to execute the
lease amendment in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: This lease is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA
Guidelines Section 15301.)
PUBLIC COMMENT
Members of the public wishing to comment on any item not appearing on the agenda may address the City Council at this time. State
law prevents Council from taking action on any matter not on the agenda; your comments may be referred to staff for follow up.
Public comment is limited to a total of 15 minutes; however, an opportunity for additional public comment may be provided later in
the agenda.
 
OLD BUSINESS
25.
Community Relations Commission Amendment – Ordinance Introduction
Introduce an Ordinance to amend the San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 2.21 "Community Relations
Commission" to incorporate diversity, equity, and inclusion issues or topics into the scope of work of the
6 of 407

--- page 7 ---
commission.
CEQA: This ordinance amendment introduction is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or
administrative activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA
Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
26.
Youth Commissioners – Ordinance Introduction
Introduce an ordinance to amend San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 2.15 “Library Board,” Chapter 2.28
“Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission,” and Chapter 2.29 “Senior Citizens Commission” to provide for
Council appointment of two non-voting youth advisory members to each of these entities.
CEQA: This ordinance introduction is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it
will not cause a physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
NEW BUSINESS
27.
2000 S. Delaware Street Affordable Housing Development Transfer to MidPen Housing - Reassignment and
Amendment of Ground Lease and Conditional Loan Commitment Term Sheet
Approve: (1) a reassignment of the ground lease for the affordable housing project at 2000 S. Delaware Street
from Westlake Reality Group to MP 2000 Delaware, LLC and amendments to the ground lease to deepen the
affordability of the units in the Project to households at or below 80% of Area Median Income; and authorize the
City Manager to execute the reassigned and amended ground lease in substantially the form provided; (2) a Term
Sheet that includes a conditional loan commitment of $500,000 in exchange for deepening the affordability of
the 60 rental units in the Project from moderate to low-income; and direct staff to return to City Council by end
of November with a regulatory agreement, loan agreement, and other documents required to fulfill the
commitments in the Term Sheet, for City Council approval.
CEQA: This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a
physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
REPORTS AND ANNOUNCEMENTS
City Manager, City Attorney and Council Members report on their various assignments and liaison roles and Council requests for
scheduling future items.
 
CLOSED SESSION
The public will have an opportunity to comment before the Council’s consideration of this item. Following the meeting a report of
action from Closed Session will be provided if required.
 
28.
Conference with Legal Counsel – Existing Litigation
(Paragraph (1) of subdivision (d) of Government Code Section 54956.9)
Name of Case: Interstate Grading and Paving, Inc. v. City of San Mateo, San Mateo Superior Court Case No.: 23-
CIV-05188
ADJOURNMENT

AGENDAS: Agendas and material are posted on the City’s website on the Friday preceding each Council Meeting and can be viewed on the City's
website at www.cityofsanmateo.org . Any supplemental material distributed to the Council after the posting of the agenda will be made part of the
official record.

WATCHING A MEETING ON TV: City Council meetings are broadcast live on Comcast/channel 27, Wave/channel 26, or AT&T/channel 99.
For transmission problems during the broadcast, please call (650) 522-7099. For all other broadcast comments, call (650) 522-7040, Monday-Friday,
8 a.m. - 5 p.m.
WATCHING A MEETING ON A COMPUTER: There are three ways to stream.
1) Public Meeting Portal www.cityofsanmateo.org/publicmeetings
2) City YouTube channel and stream it on YouTube: http://youtube.com/CityofSanMateo
3) Watch TV live stream: https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/193/Channel-San-Mateo-Live-Stream 
PUBLIC COMMENTS/REQUEST TO SPEAK
Prior to the Meeting 
Send comments to: clerk@cityofsanmateo.org until 4 p.m. the day of the meeting.
During the meeting
By Zoom: Click the link at the top of the agenda and you’ll be added to the meeting. All attendees are muted by default. When the item of interest
is open for consideration, select the “Raise Your Hand” icon and you will be called on at the appropriate time.
By telephone: Call (408) 638-0968 and enter the conference ID found at the top of the meeting agenda. When the item of interest is open for
consideration, select *9 to raise your hand. When called upon, press *6 to unmute, state your name and provide your comments.
In Person: At the meeting complete a “Request to Speak” form, submit a request at the speaker kiosk or scan the QR code.
ACCESSIBILITY: In compliance with the Americans with Disabilities Act, those with disabilities requiring special accommodations to participate in
this meeting may contact the City Clerk’s Office at (650) 522-7040 or clerk@cityofsanmateo.org . Notification 48 hours prior to the meeting will
enable the City to make reasonable arrangements to ensure accessibility to this meeting.

August 19, 2024 
SUBJECT:
State Route 82/State Route 92 Interchange Landscaping Improvements Project – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with Marina Landscape, Inc. for the State Route 82/State Route 92 Interchange Landscaping 
Improvements Project in the amount of $1,650,150; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $250,000; and 
authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders 
as allowed by the contract documents and within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
In August 2018, roadway improvements to reconfigure the State Route 82/State Route 92 Interchange (82/92 Interchange
Project) were completed as part of a joint project between the City, San Mateo County Transportation
Authority (SMCTA), and Caltrans. The original 82/92 Interchange Project included landscaping scope of work; however, 
prior to completion, the landscaping portion of the 82/92 Interchange Project was postponed by Caltrans due to the 
drought in California. Since then, the drought restrictions have been lifted.
In December 2020, the City entered into a cooperative agreement with Caltrans for the SR 82/SR 92 Interchange 
Landscaping Improvements Project (Landscaping Project) in order to implement landscaping improvements within Caltrans 
right-of-way. The Landscaping Project’s objective is to create an attractive interchange that meets Caltrans requirements 
and minimizes the resources needed to maintain it. The Landscaping Project includes clearing and grubbing, light grading 
and contouring, ground cover and tree planting, and irrigation improvements. It also includes landscaping along the sound 
wall in the northeast portion of the cloverleaf that faces the Hayward Park neighborhood. 
The City issued a request for proposals for engineering and landscaping design services on May 31, 2019. On September 3, 
2019, City Council approved an agreement with BKF Engineers to design and develop construction documents for the 
Landscaping Project.
On August 5, 2021, the SMCTA Board of Directors allocated $1.35 million of Measure A funds for the Landscaping Project. 
On March 21, 2022, City Council approved a funding agreement between the City and SMCTA to secure the $1.35 million 
for the construction phase of the Landscaping Project.    
The Landscaping Project was advertised on May 30, 2024. A total of three (3) bids were received and opened on June 27, 
2024. The bids received are listed below in order of increasing bid amount. 
Contractor
Base Bid Amount
Additive Bid Item 
A
Additive Bid Item 
B
Total Bid Amount
Marina Landscape, Inc.
$1,539,650.00

$2,123,212.84
 
Per the Contract Book, bids were compared based on the total bid amount, which includes the Base Bid plus two (2) 
additive bid items, Additive Bid Item A and Additive Bid Item B. Additive Bid Items A and B include plant maintenance and 
water use during Years 4 and 5, respectively, after the initial three years of plant establishment period covered in the base 
bid. Staff reviewed the lowest bid submitted by Marina Landscape, Inc., and determined that Marina Landscape, Inc. is the 
lowest responsive, responsible bidder. Staff recommends City Council award the Agreement to Marina Landscape, Inc. 
inclusive of the scopes of Additive Bid Items A and B based on Marina Landscape, Inc.’s pricing. In addition, staff 
recommends a 15% contingency be established given potential unforeseen site conditions and caution that will need to be 
exercised due to the project’s proximity to two State Highways.
Construction is anticipated to begin Fall 2024 and be complete by first quarter of 2025, followed by a 5-year plant 
establishment period until 2030. Traffic impacts will primarily involve installation of temporary concrete barriers along 
State Route 92 during nighttime hours, with lane closures restricted to one lane at a time. While the shoulders of on and 
off-ramps will be temporarily closed during construction, lane widths on these ramps will remain unaffected. No traffic 
control measures are anticipated along State Route 82.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There are sufficient funds in the El Camino at Highway 92 Landscaping Improvements Project (460037) to fund this work in 
the amount of $1,650,150 and the contingency reserve in the amount of $250,000.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The landscaping scope of work received environmental clearance when the project level initial study and negative 
declaration for the 82/92 Interchange Project was approved in May 2014. Environmental clearance for the Landscaping 
Project has been re-validated by Caltrans on September 2, 2021.
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
Central Recreation Center Roof Improvements – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution approving an alternative purchasing procedure to award an agreement with McGinnis Chen Associates, 
Inc. for design professional services in an amount not to exceed $93,025; establish a contingency reserve of $10,000; and 
authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue amendments 
within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Central Recreation Center at Central Park has served the community for over sixty-five years. The building’s roof 
structure consists of flat gravel and sloped wood shingle. The wood shingle has been subjected to decades of moisture and 
leaks which have been an on-going issue at the facility for years. Currently, there are water penetrations in various 
locations.
In 2023, the City engaged McGinnis Chen Associates, Inc. (MCA) to perform a Citywide roof assessment. The final report 
identified this specific location as a potential health and safety risk due to the compromised roof structure and 
recommends immediate action.  Other facilities identified with having similar issues include the Beresford Recreation 
Center, Martin Luther King Recreation Center and City Hall.
Due to the immediate need for improvements to the roof at the Central Recreation Center, City staff considered an 
alternate purchasing procedure whereby the City requested a proposal from an engineering firm that the City prequalified 
based on recent, satisfactory, and similar services received at other City facilities such as the Police Department and the 
Transit Center where MCA was tasked with the assessment, investigation, destructive testing, and design improvements 
for remediation.  The scope of services for the Central Recreation Center Roof Improvements project includes 
investigation, testing, design, documentation, bidding support, and construction administration.
An alternative purchasing method may be utilized in accordance with Municipal Code section 3.60.070(h)(3), which states 
“The following procedures may be used only upon a finding by the City Council prior to or concurrent with the award of 
contract that the procedures are in the best interests of the City for the particular contract…” 
The deterioration of the roof at the Central Recreation Center presents a high risk for biological growth which affects the 
air quality and threatens public health. Initiating the design for the improvements at the earliest time, through the 
alternate purchasing method, is recommended to be in the best interests of the City and its constituents. Based on MCA’s 
familiarity of the City’s Facilities through the Citywide Roof Assessment project, procuring MCA will result in a timely 
deliverable which allows the City to obtain building permits and award the construction in the Spring of 2025.  The 
32 of 407

--- page 33 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
construction duration is expected to take six months and can only occur during dry weather, so it is vital that the design 
documents are complete, and permits are obtained prior to that time.
MCA submitted a proposal on June 24, 2024, that includes design tasks to improve the roof at the Central Recreation 
Center.  Based on their proposal, award of the design professional services agreement to MCA is recommended.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is sufficient funding in the Central Recreation Center: Roof Replacement (46F042) project budget to fund this 
agreement and the proposed contingency reserve.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15301.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

CITY OF SAN MATEO 
RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2024) 
 
APPROVING AN ALTERNATIVE PURCHASING PROCEDURE TO AWARD AN AGREEMENT TO MCGINNIS CHEN 
ASSOCIATES, INC. FOR THE CENTRAL RECREATION CENTER ROOF IMPROVEMENTS PROJECT 
WHEREAS, San Mateo Municipal Code section 3.60.070(h)(3) provides that the City may use any 
purchasing procedure approved by the City Council if there is a finding concurrent with the award of the 
contract that the procedures are in the best interest of the City; and 
WHEREAS, the Central Recreation Center at Central Park has served the community for over sixty-five 
years, and the building’s roof structure consists of flat gravel and sloped wood shingle; and
WHEREAS, the wood shingle has been subjected to decades of moisture and leaks which have been an 
on-going issue at the facility for years resulting in water penetrations in various locations and biological growth 
under the exterior roof eaves; and
WHEREAS, in 2023, the City engaged McGinnis Chen Associates, Inc. (MCA) to perform a Citywide roof 
assessment, and the final report identified the Central Recreation Center as a potential health and safety risk 
due to the compromised roof structure and recommends immediate action; and
WHEREAS, the deterioration of the roof at the Central Recreation Center presents a high risk for 
biological growth which affects the air quality and threatens public health; and
WHEREAS, initiating the design for the improvements at the earliest time through an alternative 
purchasing procedure is recommended to be in the best interests of the City; and
WHEREAS, MCA submitted a proposal on June 24, 2024, to design improvements to the roof at the 
Central Recreation Center, and design tasks include testing, investigation, design, documentation, bidding 
support, and construction administration; and
WHEREAS, MCA is familiar with City facilities and will produce a timely deliverable that allows the City to 
obtain permits, bid and award the project efficiently; and
WHEREAS, the project requires construction to occur during dry weather only, therefore permitting, 
bidding and award of the contract will occur prior to the Spring of 2025; and
WHEREAS, MCA has performed identical work at other City facilities that require roof improvements and 
City staff believes their experience to be valuable, and their price reasonable and consistent with their previous 
work; and
WHEREAS, the City Council recognizes the need to perform roof improvements at the Central Recreation 
Center to meet the public health and safety needs of the City of San Mateo and dedicated funding for the 
Central Recreation Center Roof Replacement (46F042) in the Fiscal Year 2024-2025 Adopted Budget; and
WHEREAS, based on the above, City staff recommends approval of the agreement with McGinnis Chen 
Associates, Inc. for Central Recreation Center Roof Improvements.
34 of 407

--- page 35 ---
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY FINDS AND 
RESOLVES that: 
 
1. In accordance with CEQA Guidelines section 15301, this project is categorically exempt from CEQA as 
an ‘existing facility’ in that it involves the maintenance of an existing facility with no expansion of 
existing or former use.
2. In accordance with Municipal Code section 3.60.070(h)(3), the approval of an agreement with MCA is 
in the best interest of the City because: 
a)
Time is of the essence to complete the improvements to prevent further roof deterioration 
affecting or threatening the public health, safety, or welfare; and 
b)
Having performed a citywide roof assessment, MCA therefore has familiarity with the 
Central Recreation Center roof which will assist in timely delivery of the design; and 
c)
MCA, as the design engineer, has prior experience working on other City facilities and staff 
has been satisfied with their work; and
d)
Staff finds the proposal to be reasonable.
3. The agreement with McGinnis Chen Associates, for the Central Recreation Center Roof 
Improvements in the amount of $93,025 is approved.
4. The Public Works Director is authorized to execute the agreement in substantially the form 
submitted and issue change orders per the contract documents and within the contingency amount, 
on behalf of the City.

This Agreement, made and entered into this day of ____________________, by and between 
the CITY OF SAN MATEO, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California 
(“CITY”), and MCGINNIS CHEN ASSOCIATES, INC., a Corporation (“CONSULTANT”), whose address is 
1019 Mission Street, San Francisco, CA 94103:
RECITALS:
A.
CITY desires certain design consulting services hereinafter described.
B.
CITY desires to engage CONSULTANT to provide these design consulting services by 
reason of its qualifications and experience for performing such services and CONSULTANT has offered 
to provide the required services on the terms and in the manner set forth herein.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS AGREED as follows:
SECTION 1 - SCOPE OF SERVICES
The scope of services to be performed by CONSULTANT under this Agreement is as described in 
Exhibit A to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - DUTIES OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for the professional quality, technical accuracy and 
coordination of all work furnished by CONSULTANT under this Agreement.  CONSULTANT shall, without 
additional compensation, correct or revise any errors or deficiencies in its work.
CONSULTANT represents that it is qualified to furnish the services described under this 
Agreement.
CONSULTANT shall be responsible for employing or engaging all persons necessary to perform 
the services of CONSULTANT.
CONSULTANT agrees to comply with the City’s minimum wage ordinance as codified in 
Municipal Code Chapter 5.92, which differs from the state minimum wage and includes a Consumer 
Price Index escalator.
SECTION 3 - DUTIES OF CITY
CITY shall provide pertinent information regarding its requirements for the project.

CITY shall examine documents submitted by CONSULTANT and shall render decisions pertaining 
thereto promptly, to avoid unreasonable delay in the progress of CONSULTANT's work.
SECTION 4 - TERM
The services to be performed under this Agreement shall commence on September 1, 2024 and 
be completed on or about June 30, 2026.
SECTION 5 - PAYMENT
Payment shall be made by CITY only for services rendered and upon submission of a payment 
request upon completion and CITY approval of the work performed.  In consideration for the full 
performance of the services set forth in Exhibit A, CITY agrees to pay CONSULTANT a fee in an amount 
of $93,025, pursuant to rates stated in Exhibit B to this Agreement, attached and incorporated by 
reference.
SECTION 6 - TERMINATION
Without limitation to such rights or remedies as CITY shall otherwise have by law, CITY shall have 
the right to terminate this Agreement or suspend work on the Project for any reason, upon ten (10) days' 
written notice to CONSULTANT.  CONSULTANT agrees to cease all work under this Agreement upon 
receipt of said written notice.
Upon termination and upon CITY's payment of the amount required to be paid, documents 
become the property of CITY, and CONSULTANT shall transfer them to CITY upon request without 
additional compensation.
SECTION 7 - OWNERSHIP OF DOCUMENTS
All documents prepared by CONSULTANT in the performance of this Agreement, although 
instruments of professional service, are and shall be the property of CITY, whether the project for 
which they are made is executed or not.
SECTION 8 - CONFIDENTIALITY
All reports and documents prepared by CONSULTANT in connection with the performance of 
this Agreement are confidential until released by CITY to the public.  CONSULTANT shall not make any 
such documents or information available to any individual or organization not employed by 
CONSULTANT or CITY without the written consent of CITY before any such release.
SECTION 9 - INTEREST OF CONSULTANT
CONSULTANT covenants that it presently has no interest, and shall not acquire any interest, 
direct or indirect, financial or otherwise, which would conflict in any manner or degree with the 
performance of the services under this Agreement.

SECTION 11 - INDEMNITY
Design Professional Services: CONSULTANT agrees to hold harmless and indemnify CITY, its 
elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents from and against any and all claims, loss,

extent permitted by Civil Code section 2782.8, CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and 
appointed officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. The CONSULTANT’S duty to 
indemnify shall survive expiration or early termination of this Agreement.
Non-Design Professional Consultant Services: CONSULTANT agrees to hold harmless and 
indemnify CITY, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents from and against any and all 
claims, loss, liability, damage, and expense arising out of CONSULTANT’s performance of this 
Agreement for all services other than design professional services, except those claims arising out of 
CITY’s sole negligence or willful misconduct. CONSULTANT agrees to defend City, its elected and 
appointed officials, employees, and agents against any such claims. The CONSULTANT’S duty to 
indemnify shall survive expiration or early termination of this Agreement.

thereafter (five years for building or major improvements) the insurance specified in Exhibit C to this 
Agreement.
SECTION 13 - NONASSIGNABILITY
Both parties hereto recognize that this Agreement is for the personal services of CONSULTANT 
and cannot be transferred, assigned, or subcontracted by CONSULTANT without the prior written 
consent of CITY.

SECTION 15 - WAIVERS
The waiver by either party of any breach or violation of any term, covenant, or condition of this 
Agreement or of any provisions of any ordinance or law shall not be deemed to be a waiver of such

other money which may become due hereunder shall not be deemed to be a waiver of any preceding

applicable law or ordinance.
SECTION 16 – SEVERABILITY
If any term or portion of this Agreement is held to be invalid, illegal, or otherwise 
unenforceable by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remaining provisions of this Agreement shall 
continue in full force and effect.
SECTION 17 - COSTS AND ATTORNEY FEES
Attorney fees in total amount not exceeding $5000, shall be recoverable as costs (by the filing 
of a cost bill) by the prevailing party in any action or actions to enforce the provisions of this 
Agreement.  The above $5000 limit is the total of attorney fees recoverable whether in the trial court, 
appellate court, or otherwise, and regardless of the number of attorneys, trials, appeals, or actions.  It 
is the intent of this Agreement that neither party shall have to pay the other more than $5000 for 
attorney fees arising out of an action, or actions to enforce the provisions of this Agreement.
SECTION 18 - NON-DISCRIMINATION
CONSULTANT warrants that it is an Equal Opportunity Employer and shall comply with 
applicable regulations governing equal employment opportunity.  Neither CONSULTANT nor any of its 
sub-consultants shall discriminate in the employment of any person because of race, color, national 
origin, ancestry, physical handicap, medical condition, marital status, sex, or age, unless based upon a 
bona fide occupational qualification pursuant to the California Fair Employment and Housing Act.

SECTION 19 - MEDIATION
Should any dispute arise out of this Agreement, any party may request that it be submitted to 
mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the State Mediation and 
Conciliation Service, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.
SECTION 20 - LITIGATION
CONSULTANT shall testify at CITY's request if litigation is brought against CITY in connection 
with CONSULTANT's services under this Agreement.  Unless the action is brought by CONSULTANT, or 
is based upon CONSULTANT's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate CONSULTANT for preparation for 
testimony, testimony, and travel at CONSULTANT's standard hourly rates at the time of actual 
testimony.

EXHIBIT C
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if CONSULTANT 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than 
$1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease. 
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONSULTANT’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONSULTANT maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall 
be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.
Notice of Cancellation
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City. If a Notice 
of Cancellation endorsement is not available, CONSULTANT shall ensure the requisite Notice of

requisite notice as specified in this Exhibit C. 
Waiver of Subrogation
CONSULTANT hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
CONSULTANT may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
CONSULTANT agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a waiver of 
subrogation endorsement from the insurer.  
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the CONSULTANT to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof 
of ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within 
the retention.

endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the CONSULTANT’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

SUBJECT:
1001 Haddon Drive Ponding Repair – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with W.R. Forde Associates, Inc. for 1001 Haddon Drive Ponding Repair Project in the amount of 
$163,415.00; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $24,500; and authorize the Public Works Director to 
execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders as allowed by the contract documents 
and within the amount of the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
In October 2022, residents alerted the City to significant settlement occurring along the sidewalk, curb, gutter, and 
roadway in front of 1001 Haddon Drive. The 1001 Haddon Drive Ponding Repair (Project) will repair the settlement and 
associated ponding along with the sidewalk and curb at this location with an Engineer’s Estimate for the Project of 
$184,950.00.
 
The project was advertised on May 6, 2024, and a total of three (3) bids were received and opened on June 4, 2024. The 
bids received are listed below in order of increasing bid amount.
 
Contractor
Grand Total Bid Amount
W.R. Forde Associates, Inc.
$163,415.00
Golden Bay Construction, Inc. 
$188,544.00
Raposo Engineering, Inc.
$242,468.60
 
After review of bid documents, staff determined that W.R. Forde Associates, Inc. is the lowest responsive, responsible 
bidder. Therefore, staff recommends W.R. Forde Associates, Inc. be awarded this construction agreement. Staff also 
recommend a 15% contingency to be established given the small size of the construction agreement as well as the 
uncertainty of the stability of underlying soils on these streets. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are available in the Citywide Street Rehabilitation Package 2 (467008) project budget to award this work in 
the amount of $163,415.00 and the contingency reserve of $24,500.00.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:

and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement. The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

Exhibit A 
Insurance Requirements for Construction Contracts
Contractor shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract, and for x years thereafter, 
insurance against claims for injuries to persons or damages to property which may arise from or in 
connection with the performance of the work hereunder by the Contractor, his agents, 
representatives, employees, or subcontractors. 
MINIMUM SCOPE AND LIMIT OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 covering CGL 
on an “occurrence” basis, including products and completed operations, property damage, bodily 
injury and personal & advertising injury with limits no less than $5,000,000 per occurrence. If a 
general aggregate limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this 
project/location (ISO CG 25 03 or 25 04) or the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required 
occurrence limit.  
2. Automobile Liability:  Insurance Services Office Form CA 0001 covering Code 1 (any auto), with 
limits no less than $5,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
3. Workers’ Compensation insurance as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, 
and Employers’ Liability insurance with a limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. 
4. Surety Bonds as described below.
5. Contractors’ Pollution Legal Liability and/or Asbestos Legal Liability and/or Errors and Omissions 
(if project involves environmental hazards) with limits no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or 
claim, and $2,000,000 policy aggregate.
If the contractor maintains broader coverage and/or higher limits than the minimums shown above, 
the Entity requires and shall be entitled to the broader coverage and/or higher limits maintained by 
the contractor. Any available insurance proceeds in excess of the specified minimum limits of insurance 
and coverage shall be available to the Entity.
Self-Insured Retentions 
Self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the Entity. At the option of the Entity, 
either: the contractor shall cause the insurer shall to reduce or eliminate such self-insured retentions 
as respects the Entity, its officers, officials, employees, and volunteers; or the Contractor shall provide 
a financial guarantee satisfactory to the Entity guaranteeing payment of losses and related 
investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses. The policy language shall provide, or be 
endorsed to provide, that the self-insured retention may be satisfied by either the named insured or 
Entity.
Other Insurance Provisions 
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
1. The Entity, its officers, officials, employees, and volunteers are to be covered as additional 
insureds on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations performed 
by or on behalf of the Contractor including materials, parts, or equipment furnished in connection 
with such work or operations and automobiles owned, leased, hired, or borrowed by or on behalf

SUBJECT:
731 and 771 Crystal Springs Road Access Easements – Acceptance
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt Resolutions to accept two Grants of Easement on 731 Crystal Springs Road and 771 Crystal Springs Road; and 
authorize the City Manager to execute the Grants of Easement in substantially the form presented. 
BACKGROUND:
A Public Utility Easement (PUE) for City of San Mateo storm drain infrastructure currently exists between Columbia Drive 
and Crystal Springs Road. The PUE is 10 feet wide and existing City storm drain infrastructure extends outside of the PUE 
and into the southern corner of the property located at 731 Crystal Springs Road and northern corner of the property 
located at 771 Crystal Springs Road. The Columbia/Crystal Springs Storm Drain Improvements Project (Project) will remove 
the existing storm drain infrastructure, which currently comprises an open channel on 731 Crystal Springs Road and 
underground pipe and manhole on 771 Crystal Springs Road and replace the existing open channel and underground pipe 
and manhole with a new underground pipe, a cleanout, and manhole. Construction is expected to occur in Summer or Fall 
2024.  
Due to existing site constraints, Public Works seeks to adjust the existing alignment for new storm drain construction.  The 
location of the new underground pipe, cleanout, and manhole require the property owners at 731 Crystal Springs Road 
and 771 Crystal Springs Road to grant easements to the City of San Mateo to account for the storm drain infrastructure 
which extends outside of the current PUE. 
The property owner at 731 Crystal Springs Road agrees to grant an easement to the City of San Mateo on, across, and over 
the southern corner of their property not covered by the PUE for construction and maintenance of the storm drain 
infrastructure.
The property owner of 771 Crystal Springs Road agrees to grant an access easement to the City of San Mateo on, across, 
and over the northern corner of their property not covered by the PUE for construction and maintenance of the storm 
drain infrastructure.
The Grants of Easement include language that allows the Grantor to relocate the easements if an alternate point of access 
is identified and agreed upon by the Grantor and City of San Mateo. The City's contracted Licensed Surveyor prepared a 
plat and legal description for the agreements. The easements allow construction and operations and maintenance staff the 
proper rights to construct and maintain the storm drain infrastructure and prevent flooding issues. Staff recommends 
Council adopt the attached Resolutions accepting the proposed access easements with associated plat and legal 
descriptions and authorizing execution by the City Manager.  
60 of 407

--- page 61 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budgetary impact for accepting the grants of access easements.

This Project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15301.)

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2024)
ACCEPTING THE GRANT OF A PUBLIC UTILITY EASEMENT
731 CRYSTAL SPRINGS ROAD, SAN MATEO, CA 94403
WHEREAS, an above-ground City storm drain channel conveys stormwater runoff from Columbia Drive 
to Crystal Springs Road through the Southern border of 731 Crystal Springs Road; and
WHEREAS, City of San Mateo Public Works staff maintains the existing storm drain channel within 731 
Crystal Springs Road to prevent flooding issues; and
WHEREAS, Public Works staff traverses 731 Crystal Springs Road to a 10-foot wide Public Utility 
Easement (PUE) along the property’s Southern border to access the storm drain channel; and
WHEREAS, the property owner of 731 Crystal Springs Road limits access to the storm drain channel to 
the portion of storm drain channel within the property not covered by the PUE; and 
WHEREAS, the City requires a public utility easement over a portion of property located at 731 Crystal 
Springs Road for current and planned storm drain infrastructure improvements; and 
WHEREAS, the property owner of 731 Crystal Springs Road agrees to grant to the City of San Mateo a 
non-exclusive easement for storm drain infrastructure (Public Utility Easement) (Exhibit A) including access, 
construction, and maintenance activities related to storm drain infrastructure on, across, and over that certain 
area of land described on Exhibit A and depicted on Exhibit B for the purpose of maintaining storm drain 
infrastructure within the Easement Area; and
WHEREAS, the City’s contracted Licensed Surveyor prepared a plat (Exhibit B) and legal description 
(Exhibit A) to allow for recordation of the Public Utility Easement; and
WHEREAS, the City’s contracted Licensed Surveyor determined the plat and legal description to be 
technically correct.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES 
that:
1.
In accordance with CEQA Guidelines section 15061(b)(3), acceptance of a Public Utility Easement is 
exempt from CEQA because it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that the grant of 
an easement for storm drain infrastructure may have a significant effect on the environment.
 
2.

731 Crystal Springs Road on behalf of the City of San Mateo, set forth in Exhibit A attached hereto.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2024)
ACCEPTING THE GRANT OF A PUBLIC UTILITY EASEMENT
771 CRYSTAL SPRINGS ROAD, SAN MATEO, CA 94403
WHEREAS, a City storm drain pipe conveys stormwater runoff from Columbia Drive to Crystal Springs 
Road through the Northern border of 771 Crystal Springs Road; and
WHEREAS, City of San Mateo Public Works staff maintains the existing storm drain pipe within 771 
Crystal Springs Road to prevent flooding issues; and
WHEREAS, Public Works staff traverses 771 Crystal Springs Road to a 10-foot wide Public Utility 
Easement (PUE) along the property’s Northern border to access the storm drain pipe; and
WHEREAS, the property owner of 771 Crystal Springs Road limits access to the storm drain pipe to the 
portion of storm drain pipe within the property not covered by the PUE; and 
WHEREAS, the City requires a public utility easement over a portion of property located at 771 Crystal 
Springs Road for current and planned storm drain infrastructure improvements; and 
WHEREAS, the property owner of 771 Crystal Springs Road agrees to grant to the City of San Mateo a 
non-exclusive easement for storm drain infrastructure (Public Utility Easement) (Exhibit A) including access, 
construction, and maintenance activities related to storm drain infrastructure on, across, and over that certain 
area of land described on Exhibit A and depicted on Exhibit B for the purpose of maintaining storm drain 
infrastructure within the Easement Area; and
WHEREAS, the City’s contracted Licensed Surveyor prepared a plat (Exhibit B) and legal description 
(Exhibit A) to allow for recordation of the Public Utility Easement; and
WHEREAS, the City’s contracted Licensed Surveyor determined the plat and legal description to be 
technically correct.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES 
that:
1.
In accordance with CEQA Guidelines section 15061(b)(3), acceptance of a Public Utility Easement is 
exempt from CEQA because it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that the grant of 
an easement for storm drain infrastructure may have a significant effect on the environment.
 
2.
The City Council hereby accepts the Grant of Public Utility Easement, from the property owner of 
771 Crystal Springs Road on behalf of the City of San Mateo, set forth in Exhibit A attached hereto. 
3.
The City Council hereby authorizes and directs the City Manager to execute the Grant of Public 
Utility Easement, set forth in Exhibit A attached hereto.
4.
The City Council hereby authorizes and direct the City Clerk to record the Grant of Public Utility 
Easement with the San Mateo County Recorder’s office.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  7
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 82-4683
File ID: 24-8915
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
August 19, 2024 
SUBJECT:
Parks and Recreation Department Field Mowers - Purchase Contract
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve an alternative purchasing procedure and approve a purchase contract with Turf Star, Inc. 
for the purchase of one (1) Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) Toro Z Master Revolution in a total amount not to 
exceed $182,782.62; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $30,000.00; and authorize the Public Works Director 
to execute the purchase contract in substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency 
amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Parks and Recreation Department, Parks Division maintains more than 200 acres of greenway in the City of San Mateo, 
regular manicuring of these fields is necessary to maintain a healthy, attractive and safe environment for the community 
to enjoy. A primary tool in maintaining these fields is the use of a highly efficient wide path mower capable of manicuring a 
12'-wide section of lawn with every lap of the mower. Additionally, the City utilizes a highly maneuverable mower capable 
of efficiently manicuring a 5'-wide section for use in areas with an array of obstructions. 
The proposed purchase of one (1) Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) Toro Z Master Revolution will replace similar 
existing lawn equipment that has exceeded its useful life with units that will provide modern, reliable, efficient, and more 
environmentally friendly technology. 
As part of the transition to a Green Fleet, staff continually research electrical options during the procurement process and 
aim to replace vehicles with alternative-fueled vehicles when available. These selected Toro models are the only viable 
option currently on the market with no equivalent electric option available. When an electric version is not available, staff 
evaluates diesel options because the City purchases renewable diesel to replace the use of fossil-based fuel. Renewable 
diesel is made from organic feedstocks and its use reduces carbon emissions. The Toro is an environmentally friendly Tier 
IV diesel engine and thus, allows the City to use renewable diesel, which is a non-fossil-based option. 
Staff utilized Sourcewell pricing through Turf Star, Inc. for the purchase of this Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z 
Master Revolution. San Mateo Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3) authorizes the City Council to approve an alternative 
purchasing procedure when it finds doing so is in the best interest of the City. Sourcewell (formerly NJPA) is a government 
organization that solicits, receives, and reviews competitive bids for various specialty equipment, including the Toro 
Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z Master Revolution. Sourcewell has conducted competitive, public bids to select vehicle 
vendors to achieve competitive pricing and has selected Turf Star Inc. Therefore, the purchase of Toro Groundsmaster 
4700 from Turf Star Inc. is in the best interest of the City because the Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z Master 
Revolution are the recommended replacement for the existing Toro lawn equipment and the City may rely on bids 
76 of 407

--- page 77 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
obtained from Sourcewell because it has solicited, received, and reviewed competitive bids for the desired Toro 
Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z Master Revolution through its cooperative purchasing program. Based on the above, staff 
recommends the purchase of this Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z Master Revolution from Turf Star Inc. 
A contingency reserve is being requested to address any price fluctuations from market instability that may occur between 
the time the original quote was submitted to the time the contract is executed. Recent findings have determined this may 
result in a 10% to 20% fluctuation. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
This purchase contract will be funded from the Vehicle and Equipment Replacement Fund. Sufficient funding is available. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This purchase is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that the 
purchase of field mowers may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 – Proposed Resolution
Att 2 – Contract

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2024)
APPROVING AN ALTERNATIVE PURCHASING PROCEDURE FOR THE PURCHASE OF ONE (1) TORO 
GROUNDSMASTER 4700 AND ONE (1) TORO Z MASTER REVOLUTION WITH TURF STAR, INC. IN THE 
AMOUNT OF $182,782.62
WHEREAS, the City Council is being asked to award a contract for the purchase of one (1) new 
Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) new Toro Z Master Revolution in the amount of $182,782.62; and
WHEREAS, San Mateo Municipal Code Section 3.60.030 generally requires competitive bidding 
for contacts of $100,000 or more; and
WHEREAS, San Mateo Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3) authorizes the City Council to 
approve alternative purchasing procedures when it is in the best interest of the City; and
WHEREAS, Sourcewell (formerly NJPA) offers services to make the government procurement 
process more efficient through cooperative purchasing: and
 WHEREAS, use of Sourcewell – Contract #031121-TTC offers competitive pricing for Toro 
Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z Master Revolution; and
WHEREAS, the one (1) Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) Toro Z Master Revolution with the 
specifications and capabilities meet the requirements of the City; and
WHEREAS, Turf Star, Inc. is the sole authorized dealership in Northern California for the Toro 
Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z Master Revolution; and
WHEREAS, Turf Star, Inc. is agreeable to fulfilling Sourcewell - Contract #031121-TTC   for the 
Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z Master Revolution; and
WHEREAS, based on these circumstances, staff recommends approval of the purchase of one (1) 
new Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) new Toro Z Master Revolution from Turf Star, Inc. because it 
is in the best interest of the City without standard competitive bid practice.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY 
RESOLVES that: 
1.
The purchase of one (1) new Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) new Toro Z Master 
Revolution is not a project subject to CEQA because it can be seen with certainty that 
there is no possibility that the purchase of field mowers may have a significant effect on 
the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
2.
In accordance with Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3), the purchase of one (1) Toro 
Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) Toro Z Master Revolution from Turf Star, Inc. based on 
pricing from Sourcewell is in the City’s best interest for these reasons:
78 of 407

--- page 79 ---
a.
Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z Master Revolution are the sole manufacturer 
for the City’s Park and Recreation Departments desired vehicle; and
b.
Sourcewell competitively bid the contracts to provide the listed vehicle and Toro 
Groundsmaster 4700 and Toro Z Master Revolution was selected; and 
c.
The City has obtained competitive pricing for one (1) Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and 
one (1) Toro Z Master Revolution through Sourcewell – Contract #031121-TTC   
which will be fulfilled by Turf Star, Inc.
3.
The procedure utilized by staff to obtain Sourcewell – Contract # 031121-TTC for the 
purchase of one (1) Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) Toro Z Master Revolution 
from Turf Star Inc. is approved in accordance with Municipal Code Section 
3.60.070(h)(3).
4.
The purchase of one (1) Toro Groundsmaster 4700 and one (1) Toro Z Master Revolution 
in the amount of $182,782.62 and establishing of a contingency reserve in the amount 
of $30,000.00 is approved.
5.
The Public Works Director is authorized to execute the purchase contract in 
substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency 
amount on behalf of the City.

This Purchase Contract (“Contract”), made and entered into this day of __________, by and

SECTION 1 - PURCHASE
The goods to be purchased from VENDOR under this Contract are described in Exhibit A to this 
Agreement, which is attached and incorporated by reference.
SECTION 2 - PRICE AND TAXES
All prices shall be as stated in this Contract and are firm and not subject to escalation.  
This purchase is subject to all California sales tax.  Municipalities are exempt from federal excise and 
transportation taxes.  Prices shall exclude these taxes.  
SECTION 3 - PAYMENT
Unless otherwise agreed in writing, payment terms shall be net thirty (30) days from date of 
receipt of invoice or acceptance of goods, whichever occurs last.  Invoices must cite the purchase order 
number to prevent delay in payment.  All invoices must be mailed to City of San Mateo, Attn:  Accounts 
Payable, 330 West 20th Avenue, San Mateo, CA 94403.
SECTION 4 - DELIVERY AND PERFORMANCE
Time is of the essence in the performance of this Contract.  If delivery of goods cannot be made 
at the specified time, VENDOR shall promptly notify the CITY of the earliest possible date for delivery.  
Notwithstanding such notice, if VENDOR for any reason fails to deliver goods within the time specified or 
to the CITY’s satisfaction the CITY may terminate this Contract or any part thereof without liability 
except for goods previously provided and accepted.  The CITY’s receipt or acceptance of all or part of a 
non-conforming delivery shall not constitute a waiver of any claim, right or remedy the CITY has under 
this Contract or applicable law.

mediation.  The parties shall meet in mediation within 30 days of a request.  The mediator shall be 
agreed to by the mediating parties; in the absence of an agreement, the parties shall each submit one 
name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, the California State Board of 
Mediation and Conciliation, or other agreed-upon service.  The mediator shall be selected by a 
"blindfolded" process.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties.  Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party.  No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation and 
making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement.  The mediation process, once commenced 
by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but not more than 
60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

VENDOR's wrongdoing, CITY shall compensate VENDOR for preparation for testimony, testimony, and 
travel at VENDOR's standard hourly rates at the time of actual testimony.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  8
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 10-4662
File ID: 24-8930
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
August 19, 2024 
SUBJECT:
Staff Augmentation Services – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a professional consultant services agreement to SNG & Associates, Inc. in an amount not to exceed $200,000; 
establish a contingency reserve of $20,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in 
substantially the form presented and issue any future amendments within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
On May 8, 2024, the Department of Public Works staff issued a request for proposals (RFP) to select qualified firms to 
provide staff augmentation services to assist the City in managing and implementing capital improvement projects and 
City facilities projects. Consultant services are needed due to the loss of multiple engineering staff within the Capital 
Improvement/Engineering division. Staff recommends SNG & Associates, Inc. (SNG) to assist with capital improvement 
projects until new engineering staff are hired.  
The City received a total of six (6) proposals that were evaluated based on the firms’ project understanding, experience 
with similar projects, and technical ability of key staff. Staff short-listed two firms and conducted interviews with each 
firm’s proposed project team. SNG was identified as the highest-ranked firm. In addition, SNG’s staff augmentation 
approach, schedule, availability, and budget all align with the City’s needs.
To manage staff augmentation services, staff will develop specific task orders, scopes of work, and budgets to be 
performed.
Based on the above, staff recommend entering into a professional consultant services agreement with SNG for staff 
augmentation services in an amount not to exceed $200,000. Additionally, staff recommends establishing a contingency 
reserve in the amount of $20,000 to cover any unforeseen costs. The proposed term of this agreement is through June 
2026.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is sufficient funding in the Capital Improvement Program Engineering Division’s operating budget and within 
individual project budgets to fund this agreement and establish the contingency reserve. As such, no additional budget 
appropriations are required.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Council action is not a project subject to CEQA review under the “common sense” exemption, because it can be seen 
with certainty that there is no possibility that the award of a staff augmentation agreement to assist the City in managing 
capital improvement projects may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
